<div id="review_1774449494" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1774449494" />
    <a title="Emma♔☯ (Bookishfix)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49475701-emma-bookishfix"><img alt="Emma♔☯ (Bookishfix)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516698685p2/49475701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1774449494?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma♔☯ (Bookishfix)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma♔☯ (Bookishfix)" href="/user/show/49475701-emma-bookishfix">Emma♔☯ (Bookishfix)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1774449494" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5175245397308031570"><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>“The world was becoming a zoo, without cages.”</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><i>End of the world, apocalypse novel, but with animals?! This actually surprised me as i didn't enjoy my last James Patterson read all that much. But this, being a standalone, i enjoyed it immensely. So many reviewed this really low, maybe due to the fact that many animal activists hate animals being seen as dangerous and out of control, even in a novel. I love animals(hello, im living with 4 cats, and a dog atm) and hate seeing any animal </i></span>
  <span id="freeText5175245397308031570" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>“The world was becoming a zoo, without cages.”</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><br><i>End of the world, apocalypse novel, but with animals?! This actually surprised me as i didn't enjoy my last James Patterson read all that much. But this, being a standalone, i enjoyed it immensely. So many reviewed this really low, maybe due to the fact that many animal activists hate animals being seen as dangerous and out of control, even in a novel. I love animals(hello, im living with 4 cats, and a dog atm) and hate seeing any animal hurt ,harmed or mistreated. This book showed both human and animal deaths quite frequently throughout so its not like the animals are being picked on. I can only imagine this book having had hordes of PETA enthusiasts marching and stating James Patterson is trying to corrupt our minds , or build on our fear of animals. Remember that it is fiction, meaning it's not real, made up from the author's imagination. So calm the fuck down for a second and enjoy the book for what it is, an author's imagination coming to life on paper.<br>Sometimes i think we as human, take some things far too seriously than we are meant to, while other major issues in life get brushed aside like they are nothing.<br>Confusing breed we are sometimes.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427797620ra/14321939.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Jackson Oz is a biologist, studying the unusual spike in abnormal behaviour and aggression displayed in animals over the past years. Having quit from college, due to many thinking of him as loon, he studies and puts all his time and effort into developing a theory known as HAC- Human Animal Conflict. The bases of the theory is that something on an large environmental scale has triggered the animals to change their normal animalistic behaviour and become hyper-aggressive resulting in multiple calculated attacks on humans. <br>Having to leave his rescue monkey, Attila behind and head to Africa to study and capture evidence of HAC, Oz meets and rescues, ecologist Chloe Tousignant. Together they must disclose to the world what Oz has worked on and been ridiculed for years. Opening the eyes of millions and those in government with the power to act may be harder than they thought, but with the increasing danger the world and the human population is under, what else do they have to lose?<br><br>Okay first of all, all the death scenes weather animal or human were really well thought out and detailed. If you don't like this gruesome stuff, this book isn't for you. We have lion attacks, rodent attacks, mauling's , shootings, intestines ripped out, the whole lot. But once again, it is a end of the world, apocalypse novel about animals going wild against humans, as if you weren't expecting this..<br>The change in animal behaviour is not only shown from beginning to end, it also explains how the animal should normally respond/behave, making it a really interesting read. This had me like:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452846319ra/17750085.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I liked Jackson Oz as a main character, he is really smart and stands up for what he believes in even when his colleagues and those with a PHD put him down and call him a loon. To stand alone, and try to do your best for humanity even behind closed doors, without much power to change anything but try to get those who can to listen is amazing; his will to fight/save is truly captivating.<br>I especially loved that he rescued Attila from a testing lab, and made a home for him in his apartment. It was cute how he would interact with Attila as though he were a small child, and you could see that he loved him, even stating that when he grew too big and too hard to look after he would find him a home in a sanctuary so he could receive the care , space and love he would need to live a content life. Plus with lines like this, how could you not love his character? I literally laughed.<br><blockquote><b>“It was like crawling into the asshole of Satan.”</b></blockquote>
<br><br>My only real problem was the ending, i needed more from it hence my rating. It just kind of ended out of nowhere. We had a solution to the problem, but nothing had necessarily changed, it went back to being a shit storm and the humans having to try and survive. That was a little bit of a let down, but the rest was awesome! I'm not sure if their will be another book, or an add on or something in a few years times.<br>I know its been made into a series on Netflix but from reviews I've seen, its very different to the book and alot said it was quite boring and dull.<br><br>If you can get passed the gruesome deaths, and not take the animals gone crazy too seriously, then give this book as go. I was surprised by it and so may you.<br><br><b>Recommended for: Sci-Fi/ Apocalyptic / Zoology/Fiction /Mild Romance<br><br></b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5175245397308031570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/429985044" />
    <a title="Linda Munro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4285637-linda-munro"><img alt="Linda Munro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356960454p2/4285637.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/429985044?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda Munro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda Munro" href="/user/show/4285637-linda-munro">Linda Munro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer429985044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9468046151408386963"> I have to admit that I am like every other James Patterson fan, I see his name as author of a book and I have to read it; but, haven't you wondered how much of these books with co-authors are actually written by him? Since the style of this book is identical to the Michael Bennett books co-authored by Michael Ledwidge, and so dissimilar to the style of other Patterson books, let's finally give credit where credit is due... Ledwidge is brilliant! After all, who else knows how to slip just the ri</span>
  <span id="freeText9468046151408386963" style="display:none"> I have to admit that I am like every other James Patterson fan, I see his name as author of a book and I have to read it; but, haven't you wondered how much of these books with co-authors are actually written by him? Since the style of this book is identical to the Michael Bennett books co-authored by Michael Ledwidge, and so dissimilar to the style of other Patterson books, let's finally give credit where credit is due... Ledwidge is brilliant! After all, who else knows how to slip just the right touch of humor into a terrifying situation?<br /> Since the running idea deals with animals amassing and attacking, it's really not a good idea to have the Discovery Channel's "When animals attack" playing in the background. The plot however deals with cause and effect, and people in the know who are shunned as doomsday prophets, until the situation demands attention. <br /> Unlike most of the Patterson books, this novel actually has a moral (ignore any scientific theory until devestation faces you to admit there is something to the theory) as well as significant lesson concerning human perspicacity (as in 99.9% of all humans seem to lack it). Of course, I refuse to write a spoiler, so you'll have to read the book (all the way to the end) to figure out what I mean! <br /><br />Update, because of the television series I decided to reread this book. Why is it that books are never as you remember them? <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="9468046151408386963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1640801449?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alaina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alaina" href="/user/show/50620706-alaina">Alaina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1640801449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6947867380596407735">I've read books by James Patterson before so I was kind of hesitant to read this book after watching the first season of the TV show that is sort of based on this book. Hesitant because I didn't want to end up disliking the book because the show was just meh to me. <br/><br/>After reading it, the book was meh to me. The writing was okay but the characters seemed to annoy the crap out of me. Jackson Oz, the young biologist trying to figure out why animals are attacking humans was just an ass and sometimes </span>
  <span id="freeText6947867380596407735" style="display:none">I've read books by James Patterson before so I was kind of hesitant to read this book after watching the first season of the TV show that is sort of based on this book. Hesitant because I didn't want to end up disliking the book because the show was just meh to me. <br /><br />After reading it, the book was meh to me. The writing was okay but the characters seemed to annoy the crap out of me. Jackson Oz, the young biologist trying to figure out why animals are attacking humans was just an ass and sometimes did or said something stupid. God, I hated him throughout the book which makes sense since I didn't like him on the show either. Plus a lot of scenes didn't really make sense to me. Like how could a one eye lion see with both eyes? Did the missing eye magically come back while attacking people? I'm so confused!<br /><br />Besides Oz, there was Chloe who didn't really do anything in the book. It's like.. what was the point of having her in the book? Then the whole ending and the reason why they were attacking people was stupid. This book honestly made me so mad and it also made me not want to continue watching the show either. <br /><br />I think I need a break from James Patterson books because I have just been getting mad at them. I want a happy book.<br /><br />Overall, it was meh. I will never reread it. I have no idea if I want to read the next book. I kind of wish I never knew this was a book.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6947867380596407735" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HWW3Xb16w7n7Cy7+udjUQhRmTiKBzT4jm+EV9cyf0fGYuuPSs/FiV8ENDBGB8F3ljF4Qlp4raced/8oDI9GrIA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2sjfAIgI2MirDvHVZYfJCwPj5YuQoxVcdJ0vf8fq4qpfF4uPhoN5JpEI0zpdr0Csm9u7P49FQrhyg/CJKKSYew==')})
  }

He was in the middle of planting impatiens in the yard of one of his clients when his cell phone rang. Now he\'s standing in a normal suburban neighborhood on a bright summer day, having a phone conversation out of his darkest nightmare. Whoever is on the other end of the line is dead serious. He has to find the two million by then. But he\'ll pay a lot more. He\'ll pay anything. From its tense opening to its shattering climax, The Husband is a thriller that will hold you in its relentless grip for every twist, every shock, every revelation...until it lets you go, unmistakably changed. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8168701178328461597"><a href='http://www.jamespatterson.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Official US Site</a><br/><a href='http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk' rel='nofollow noopener'>Official UK Site</a><br/><a href='http://jimmypatterson.org' rel='nofollow noopener'>JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br/><a href='http://readkiddoread.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>ReadKiddoRead</a><br/><br/><br/><br/>James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books wo</span>
  <span id="freeText8168701178328461597" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Official US Site</a><br /><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Official UK Site</a><br /><a href="http://jimmypatterson.org" rel="nofollow noopener">JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br /><a href="http://readkiddoread.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadKiddoRead</a><br /><br /><br /><br />James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books worldwide and currently holds the Guinness World Record for the most #1 New York Times bestsellers. In addition to writing the thriller novels for which he is best known, among them The President Is Missing with President Bill Clinton, Patterson also writes fiction for young readers of all ages, including the Max Einstein series, produced in partnership with the Albert Einstein Estate. He is also the first author to have #1 new titles simultaneously on the New York Times adult and children’s bestseller lists.<br /> <br />The son of an insurance salesman and a schoolteacher, Patterson grew up in Newburgh, New York, and began casually writing at the age of nineteen. In 1969, he graduated from Manhattan College. He was given a full-ride scholarship to Vanderbilt University’s graduate program in English. He left Vanderbilt before getting his PhD due to complications involving the Vietnam War. <br /> <br />Instead, he moved to New York to become a junior copywriter for the advertising agency J. Walter Thompson, eventually becoming CEO of its North American company.<br /> <br />In 1976, while still working for J. Walter Thompson, Patterson published his first novel, The Thomas Berryman Number, with Little, Brown and Company. After being turned down by thirty-one publishers, it won the Edgar Award for Best First Novel. Patterson’s 1993 novel, Along Came a Spider, his first book to feature Alex Cross, was also his first New York Times bestseller in fiction.<br /> <br />In 2001, Morgan Freeman starred as Alex Cross in a film adaptation of Along Came a Spider, and Tyler Perry also played the character in the 2012 film Alex Cross. A film adaptation of Patterson’s middle-grade novel Middle School: The Worst Years of My Life was released in theaters in October 2016.<br /> <br />James Patterson has donated more than one million books to students, focusing on some of the most under-resourced schools and youth programs in the country. To date, he has donated $7.25 million to school and classroom libraries throughout the United States, and $2.1 million to independent bookstores and employees.<br /> <br />Patterson has recently donated over $35 million to his and his wife’s alma maters—the University of Wisconsin, Vanderbilt University, and Manhattan College—and he has established over four hundred Teacher and Writer Education Scholarships at twenty-one colleges and universities throughout the country. Patterson has also donated more than one million books to U.S. soldiers at home and overseas.<br /> <br />In May 2015, Patterson launched a children’s book imprint at Little, Brown—JIMMY Patterson—that is unwaveringly focused on one goal: turning kids into lifelong readers. This imprint also provides resources, strategies, and programs to serve teachers, parents, librarians, and booksellers. Patterson invests proceeds from the sales of JIMMY Patterson Books in pro-reading initiatives.<br /> <br />Patterson also founded ReadKiddoRead.com, a website designed to help parents, teachers, and librarians ignite a new generation’s excitement for reading. Awarded the National Book Foundation’s Innovations in Reading Prize and the American Library Association’s Great Websites for Kids, the site features thoughtful book reviews from a variety of genres and age ranges, a large and lively Facebook community, and contributions from other authors.<br /> <br />Patterson’s awards for adult and children’s literature include the Edgar Award, the International </span>
  <a data-text-id="8168701178328461597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
